<div id="review_2249913502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2249913502" />
    <a title="Yusra  ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67405281-yusra"><img alt="Yusra  ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521992247p2/67405281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2249913502?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yusra  ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yusra  ✨" href="/user/show/67405281-yusra">Yusra  ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249913502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15206499974183998865">so I am very,,,conflicted? I mean, I just want to say that I was on my period when I read Simon Vs. & I was on my period while reading Leah and it was just a weird sync. & i honestly think the reason I was so gushy and in love with the dynamics between the characters was likely due to this fact!! but onto the review (which is basically just my ramblings)<br/><br/><b> spoilers below regarding character relationships. read the synopsis before you read my review !</b> <br/><br/>so basically, this was a two star book for me u</span>
  <span id="freeText15206499974183998865" style="display:none">so I am very,,,conflicted? I mean, I just want to say that I was on my period when I read Simon Vs. &amp; I was on my period while reading Leah and it was just a weird sync. &amp; i honestly think the reason I was so gushy and in love with the dynamics between the characters was likely due to this fact!! but onto the review (which is basically just my ramblings)<br /><br /><b> spoilers below regarding character relationships. read the synopsis before you read my review !</b> <br /><br />so basically, this was a two star book for me until the end. I’ll tell you the problem here: Leah and Abby. the two “main” characters and… i just couldn’t bring myself to like them at all. just as characters themselves, they were so bland and unlikeable. <br /><br />i loved leah so much during Simon Vs. because she just had that genuine vibe to her, and she was also such a diverse character. when reading, i was so excited to know i’d be reading this book solely about her life. but her character depth just wasn’t mind blowing like i thought it would be. you’ve probably already seen the reviews and everything; to put it plainly, she’s a bitch. but like i highkey don’t have a problem with that bc aren’t we all? but leah’s character was written like becky was trying way too hard. most of leah’s decisions are just ill-timed and don’t necessarily make sense. for ex, she gets so angry at morgan for making a racist statement that wasn’t really… that racist? maybe i’m just uneducated on things in georgia but it seemed as though leah overreacted simply because of her feelings towards abby. like if it was bram that was being talked about, i doubt leah would have gone so overboard with ignoring morgan. you know what i’m saying? like all of sudden leah’s love for abby is so apparent. <br />on the other hand, i hated how rude leah was to her mother <i> with no context whatsoever </i> like her mother was so kind and loving ?? so why does leah have to take that to an advantage and just be an annoying child? <br />on the other hand i definitely loved some of the scenes with leah! when she wasn’t being rude to her mom, the dynamic they shared was so good. leah and her yellow dress were my main OTP in this entire novel, no joke. i was so proud of my girl feeling confident and beautiful and it was all done so so well. <br /><br />now, why didn’t i like abby? i honestly have no clue. just that i didn’t see what was so special about her that made everyone head over heels for her. like okay, i respect that she’s hardworking and that as a POC, she has to work even harder to break out of stereotypes people set up for her but OTHER THAN THAT… what’s to love? mm and “i thought we were just two straight girls experimenting!!” made me so mad. abby lacked character depth and building and that set off the entire mood for me. <br /><br />f/f romances are great and all, and i understand we need more of them in books. but seriously… who thought of putting leah and abby together. there was no connection between them. i just didn’t understand where all the fuss was coming from!! i was highkey skimming all their scenes together. i could rant all day about this but i’ll leave it at that, i just didn’t ship them and it’s a personal preference of mine. there was no chemistry, they didn’t make me feel any ways… a disaster. it felt forced.<br /><br />also leah was just so mean to garrett and so i don’t like her. that is all :)<br /><br />but there is a SURE REASON i’m giving this three stars! and that was because all of my other babies were ever present in this book and I LOVED THEM. like simon and blue were the perfect couple i was gushing and in love. so much cuteness at one time must be bad for my health. nick was also um really cute and i’m in love with him and he deserves better than taylor and abby COMBINED aka me (jk) (jk)<br />garrett is such a cutie, so kind to leah, so in love with leah and my girl leah leads him on. fck I HATE LEAH BECAUSE OF THIS. <br />the ending felt rushed, it felt bland, it felt tacky. it felt like becky just threw all the characters names together and said “here! have some couples. love them”. sorry girlfriend, not this time. simon and blue are the only ones that made any sense. <br />that being said, it’s senior year for our creekwood babes and considering i’m graduating in seven (!!) days, the prom scene/ending scene got me all in my feels and I <i> may </i> have shed a tear or two. if there’s one thing becky knows how to do, it’s make friendships hit close to home. simon &amp; leah were wonderful. <br /><br />it took me a whole month to read this &amp; i lent my book to a friend after 5 chaps, and that says it all, i think. <br /><br />all in all, <b> this book just isn’t as good as simon vs. and i doubt anything will ever be. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15206499974183998865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8869657952350514774">so here's some things you should know about me before i get into this:<br/>- i'm bi, and was scared to come out to friends irl for so long, even though the ones i would've told are LGBTQ<br/>- i'm. well. not on the skinny side of the weight spectrum<br/>- i am pretty bad at dealing with emotions and can sometimes come across too blunt<br/>- i doubt my own talents and abilities<br/>- unrelated, but i'm writing this while very tired<br/><br/>so you can probably see why this book made me feel so SEEN. i thought simon vs made me feel</span>
  <span id="freeText8869657952350514774" style="display:none">so here's some things you should know about me before i get into this:<br />- i'm bi, and was scared to come out to friends irl for so long, even though the ones i would've told are LGBTQ<br />- i'm. well. not on the skinny side of the weight spectrum<br />- i am pretty bad at dealing with emotions and can sometimes come across too blunt<br />- i doubt my own talents and abilities<br />- unrelated, but i'm writing this while very tired<br /><br />so you can probably see why this book made me feel so SEEN. i thought simon vs made me feel comfortable with who i am, but then its sequel came about and HOO BOY. god damn, y'all. something about seeing so many aspects of myself portrayed by a main character in a book like this made me tear up when i finished reading this. i've never really felt that way before until leah burke came along. that's something that i'm going to hold close to my heart for a long time.<br />and not to be cheesy as shit but this book also made me feel like....everything might work out for me like it kind of did for leah, y'know? like, maybe one day i'll go to a college i love and get a girlfriend and come out and people will be okay with it and i'll feel brave enough to be proud of the things i'm good at. and i don't think a book has ever made me feel that way before. so thank you, becky. thank you for simon, but thank you most of all for leah &lt;3</span>

<div id="review_2489922882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2489922882" />
    <a title="Book Roast" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58496095-book-roast"><img alt="Book Roast" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553183984p2/58496095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2489922882?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Roast" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Roast" href="/user/show/58496095-book-roast">Book Roast</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2489922882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16966559301506738441">I really loved Simon book, I really wanted to enjoy this one even though I already went in it a bit wary because Leah wasn't my favourite character from the first book (the girl on girl hate etc).<br/><br/>I hoped things will be addressed, and it sort of was but not in a way that justifies anything.<br/><br/>Leah is even more bitter, angry, mean, unreasonable and insufferable to everyone around her in this book than before. <br/><br/>I wanted to relate to her, and technically I could on many accounts, but BOI. <br/><br/>This book is a</span>
  <span id="freeText16966559301506738441" style="display:none">I really loved Simon book, I really wanted to enjoy this one even though I already went in it a bit wary because Leah wasn't my favourite character from the first book (the girl on girl hate etc).<br /><br />I hoped things will be addressed, and it sort of was but not in a way that justifies anything.<br /><br />Leah is even more bitter, angry, mean, unreasonable and insufferable to everyone around her in this book than before. <br /><br />I wanted to relate to her, and technically I could on many accounts, but BOI. <br /><br />This book is about a girl who is happy with her body and how she looks like. Except that she's not, and she then continues to also hate on everyone around her that are a different body type from her. <br /><br />She treats her friends horribly without ever explaining why and they keep trying to be nice to her. Bless them. They did their very best to keep her happy and included but she kept pushing herself away and then calling them out on it instead. At one point she straight up says she's happy her friends are miserable because they'll "know how she feels"... Wow, what a "great" friend. <br /><br />The whole plot was bitter, nothing was dealt with, she continued to be mean until she found love and this ended up being the 'love changes it all' story, RIP all single people because apparently in order to be nice to others you need to find a relationship. <br /><br />I've disliked this character a lot, and the message this book sends doesn't sit well with me. <br /><br />*Edit: also!! She uses another character simply for making herself feel wanted, she toys with this character, never explaining her true intentions AND that never bites her in the butt. I felt so utterly sorry for this person, who tried so hard and I'm sure got hurt so badly, and it NEVER get's addressed. <br /><br />Pluses: it did made me giggle few times and there were a lot of Harry Potter references :) I finished the book because we also got some glimpses of Simon &amp; 'blue', and those guys are cinnamon rolls. <br /><br />Believe me, I realise this is supposed to be representative of a lot of things but just because there's rep in the book doesn't make it automatically good and this is a prime example. <br /><br />Hope I don't have to get into my own experience growing up or my sexuality, or body shape etc to validate my opinion, which seems to be the case when you don't like something with rep. <br /><br />I'm always glad to hear somebody found value in books I didn't, if that's you - that's amazing. This one wasn't for me, however.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16966559301506738441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2294021036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2294021036" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2294021036?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-four-stars">2018-four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-audio">2018-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-ya-challenge">2018-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2294021036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3230827349550245331"><b>4 stars!!!</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525008361i/25452565._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>How much did I love <i>Leah on the Offbeat</i> by Becky Albertalli?? SO FREAKING MUCH!!! And the main reason I loved it so much was Leah Burke. She is a boss. She’s my hero. I just fucking loved her! I liked her in Simon’s book, but she really shined in her own book. What I love most about Leah is she is unapologetically herself. She never pretends to be someone she’s not and she shouldn’t have to. She is awesome just the way she is. <br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I swear, people can’t wrap their minds around the</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText3230827349550245331" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!!!</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525008361i/25452565._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>How much did I love <i>Leah on the Offbeat</i> by Becky Albertalli?? SO FREAKING MUCH!!! And the main reason I loved it so much was Leah Burke. She is a boss. She’s my hero. I just fucking loved her! I liked her in Simon’s book, but she really shined in her own book. What I love most about Leah is she is unapologetically herself. She never pretends to be someone she’s not and she shouldn’t have to. She is awesome just the way she is. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I swear, people can’t wrap their minds around the concept of a fat girl who doesn’t diet. Is it that hard to believe I might actually like my body?</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> I loved the friendships in this story, and of course the romance. Honestly, I had no idea who Leah’s love interest would be. I’m so happy that wasn’t spoiled for me, so I’m not going to spoil it for anyone else! I was surprised, but it was perfect. I loved how different the two girls were, but how they just worked. College roadtrip, sketches, Harry Potter, and PROM. Need I say more?   <br><br>And also a shout out goes to Leah’s mom. I flipping loved her. She was hilarious and she and Leah together were a hoot! My mom and I are only 16 years apart so we always had that fun, growing up together relationship, and I could definitely relate to Leah when it came to that. Their banter was great and I loved that they were both so open with each other. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Of all the fuckin’ days…”<br>“Okay, please don’t say fuckin’.”<br>She shoots me a self-conscious glance. “I thought we liked cussing.”<br>“We love cussing. But we say the fucking g. I don’t want to hear that apostrophe, mom.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Overall, this was a fantastic follow up to Simon. I recommend it to all of you who have read and loved Simon. Honestly, I would 100% recommend reading Simon before this. It could technically be read as a stand-alone, but it would be so much better if you read them both! If you’re looking for a fun, hilarious, quirky, and romantic YA read, pick this one up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3230827349550245331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1986529391?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=f-f">f-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=bi-mc">bi-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1986529391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15600940127028709473"><i>
  <blockquote>“I hate when assholes have talent. I want to live in a world where good people rule at everything and shitty people suck at everything.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>I really, really wanted to love this book. </b>It was one of my most anticipated 2018 releases, and I was so excited to get this story from Becky Albertalli. For me personally, seeing a bisexual girl in a mainstream book I knew people would read really means a lot. Unfortunately this fell very very flat to me, and I’m going to be straight up here and acknowledge</span>
  <span id="freeText15600940127028709473" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“I hate when assholes have talent. I want to live in a world where good people rule at everything and shitty people suck at everything.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>I really, really wanted to love this book. </b>It was one of my most anticipated 2018 releases, and I was so excited to get this story from Becky Albertalli. For me personally, seeing a bisexual girl in a mainstream book I knew people would read really means a lot. Unfortunately this fell very very flat to me, and I’m going to be straight up here and acknowledge this may not be my most unbiased, objective review. I brought a lot of my ideas and hopes of what this book, and what Becky Albertalli would write, into this book and I think that played a part in my disappointment.<br /><br /><b>I’m going to start with the positives.</b> I LOVED LEAH AS A MAIN CHARACTER SO MUCH. Her voice absolutely shone in this book and it dragged me into the story. Leah is a bit straight up and brash but I totally loved it, and it’s nice to see girls in YA getting more diverse, complex personalities that transcend archetypes. She, and this book in general, was also hilarious which is of course a massive plus. I seriously don't get why everyone's hating on her so much?? Like she's cool as fuck! (TEA. if she was a boy y'all would love her but people just HATE FEMALE CHARACTERS)<br /><br />As with all Becky Albtertalli books, this was very readable. Once you started with this one, it was very hard to put it down. Albteralli infuses her works with such life and fun that you can’t help fall deep into the story. Her books are un-putdown-able.<br /><br />But here’s where I get to my first issue. Compared to other Albtertalli books, I found so many parts of this book a slog. A lot of this book revolved around drama and fights and other friendship group messiness I just really could have done without. And here’s the thing: from any other author I probably wouldn’t have minded. But I expected something fluffy and fun and I just feel like instead I kinda got misery and it was annoying. I found the drama really upsetting at times.<br /><br />On that, I also felt like a lot of Leah on the Offbeat felt clunky and out of character. I often felt like aspects of Leah, including Leah’s and Abby’s backstory and how some of the characters interacted, was super out of line with Simon Vs. I want to put a note here that I saw Love, Simon before reading this and that could have influenced by perceptions. But I still felt like, overall, some of the events and drama felt really, really out of place.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Imagine going about your day knowing someone’s carrying you in their mind. That has to be the best part of being in love- the feeling of having a home in some else’s brain.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />One big aspect of this book for me was the bisexual rep. I was curious to see what it would be like and how the main f/f ship would be handled.<br /><br />I’ll say first of all I generally enjoyed the rep, up until about 3/4 through. Leah was bisexual on page, which was nice. Leah spoke about her crushes and ships and the way she mentioned both men and women was really cute. I loved that she shipped both Ninej and also Percabeth. I also liked the discussion around coming out, and how it was uncomfortable, maybe even more so since her friends were out. I also think her being bi made so much sense with Simon Vs (idk how yall missed it but like,,, she literally is the person who introduced simon to queer fanfiction and you all actually thought she was straight??)<br /><br />The f/f ship was cute, and I liked how it developed. The way that Leah spoke about the girl she was into was so soft and sweet, and it was really nice following how their relationship developed. Plus, the epilogue gave me LIFE. But again, I felt like so much of the potential aww’nesss of the relationship was ruined by the drama. The angst and mess wasn’t balanced enough for me so it was just annoying. I also HATED the first kiss and how it played out. I also think it was disappointing how many interactions with the main couple were fraught with misunderstandings and miscommunication.<br /><br />And as mentioned earlier, 3/4 through something happened which I really didn’t like. This was the discussion between Leah and her LI about being bi. I’m going to link Marianne’s review, because she goes into it more depth and echoes what I think about this scene.<br /><br />This scene was very unsettling to me. I understand what it was trying to do – point out that bisexual girls aren’t just in it for LAUGHS but that we’re actually genuinely queer, not straight girls messing around. But this scene really missed the mark. It upset me a bit, and I think it’d definitely hurt questioning people. I also think it’s just kind of wrong. Being “lowkey bi” is valid. The implication is that she’s a bit into girls, and you know what, if you’re a girl who likes girls only a little bit, that is VALID. I think this scene really, really missed the mark. And I’m actually really surprised and shocked it passed so many sensitivity readers.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I'm basically your resident fat Slytherin Rory Gilmore.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Okay, so yeah I didn't love this book, but I don't think it's bad either. It just isn't what I wanted from this book. I feel like if I reread it I might like it more upon rereading. But for me this had too many elements I didn't want and not enough I did. (OKAY FORGOT TO NOTE BUT, SIMON AND BLUE ARE CUTE)<br /><br />I don't think people should be deterred from picking this up. Becky Albertalli writes good books, this one just wasn't for me and not everything came together in a satisfying way for me. <br /><br />(on a salty side note, some of y'alls reviews for this book are disgraceful and y'all don't deserve gay girls bc you don't treat them right.)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15600940127028709473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13857101636081615545"><b>not to be dramatic but i liked this better than simon vs.</b><br/><br/>it's not that it was objectively more intriguing, or had a better plot. because honestly it didn't. but this felt so realistic and heartfelt and so very ME... i just loved it.<br/><br/>i'm not going to ramble about the plot or characters. but i want to point out how much i loved leah. she was so sarcastic and dramatic and had actual flaws. she got angry and would storm off. like... <b>we stan a realistic queen.</b> i think we often get annoyed when ya cont</span>
  <span id="freeText13857101636081615545" style="display:none"><b>not to be dramatic but i liked this better than simon vs.</b><br /><br />it's not that it was objectively more intriguing, or had a better plot. because honestly it didn't. but this felt so realistic and heartfelt and so very ME... i just loved it.<br /><br />i'm not going to ramble about the plot or characters. but i want to point out how much i loved leah. she was so sarcastic and dramatic and had actual flaws. she got angry and would storm off. like... <b>we stan a realistic queen.</b> i think we often get annoyed when ya contemporary characters have personalities like this but i think we just need to take one long ass look at ourselves and realize we're not perfect and that we're probably more like these characters than we'd care to admit.<br /><br />i will say, much like simon, i wish that the ending wasn't as abrupt as it was. i wish that the romance has blossomed just a taaaaad earlier on. and i would have liked to see just a little more development on the part of leah. it seemed like we got a lot of life tidbits about other characters but leah was just a background character in her own story. but then again, aren't we all?<br /><br />go read this if you like sarcasm, sass, and representation. this was fantastic.<br /><br />*****************<br /><br />a very <b>gay</b> buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/67405281-yusra" rel="nofollow noopener">sass queen ✨</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily" rel="nofollow noopener">pale pal ☁️</a></span>

		<td>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hrqTsRHrzgifzPLFg6GKSPUcQxNIfIA56VAPKkhLKbzEklyAhC2mhkiH7aldcDg7NTK/+QxR+3cadPKiPsHh/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QLJkJLXkhwJFy8umOsglSIq3kfdZZgnPwpJMZnUOrtQCmqsVICLvjJKA1MrkGZc7SpltHR1LcoExtrHuA4RmlA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10483098190350034619">Becky Albertalli is the author of the acclaimed novels Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda (film: Love, Simon), The Upside of Unrequited, and Leah on the Offbeat. She is also the co-author of What If It's Us with Adam Silvera. A former clinical psychologist who specialized in working with children and teens, Becky lives with her family in Atlanta. You can visit her online at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.beckyalbertalli.com'>www.beckyalbertalli.com</a>.</span>

          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
